(2017).\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty1346fig8.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/118349808/sty1346fig8.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty1346fig8.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"118349808\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/478/4/10.1093_mnras_sty1346/3/sty1346fig8.jpeg?Expires=1611465999&Signature=VtwgzqP4qjbyWyxEQVVrIHzsKT8MhjWZvZaEo5PWPflOTfmzmn3F9wE1Pw8FvKZWUDO4bawgB2x9DhPnFQc-EunTYjmmeWM84cq-rmz5WNZ6qRCwJ3vPKFGmZURvYTxDadXvQkqPpOkcxgjvoyUFbPwcx6JrTZvK4hvNlTLWpQiuRcWdXO7D~12uWMLMlgawTxFiOM2sxDAb1uAK70AOeAP13ClNNJ47SAog~JaftKi7YdngbaBRTXMRsAC6wbV5BPTpOTLOxizqJZLxGatjYkrPVJAHRWJAh6juHE2HdJVW7slT5O3wdDv4aRlA6Bgt-kEZlOqQQcf4LxofPZf8rA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=118349808&ar=5001437&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"sty1346fig8.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Histograms showing the typical magnifications for 10<sup>4</sup> microlensed supernovae for each image in iPTF16geu, around the time of <em>HST</em> imaging. The magnifications are in units of magnitudes and show the microlensing deviation from the smooth macromodel. The red dashed lines give the corresponding observations from Goobar et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>).</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">If iPTF16geu has a standard Type Ia luminosity, then at least some of the disagreement in the observed and predicted fluxes must be due to deficiencies in the macromodel. The presence of a dark substructure or a stellar disc close to image A may explain this flux anomaly (Vegetti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Hsueh et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">iPTF has an <em>r</em>-band discovery limit of 21st mag (Goobar et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>); without the extreme magnification of image A, iPTF16geu still would have been identified as a transient by iPTF, but only marginally. The transient was only added to the spectroscopic follow-up queue when the system reached an <em>r</em>-band magnitude of 19.3 (Goobar et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). iPTF16geu would likely had not been confirmed as a GLSNe Ia without the extreme magnification of image A. The demagnification of Image D is another atypical feature of iPTF16geu. Whilst microlensing can plausibly explain the observed brightness of D, the presence of dust may also contribute to the dimming. Therefore, the micro and macrolensing of iPTF16geu are therefore unlikely to be representative of a future population of lensed SNe. However, this result does demonstrate that breaking the mass-sheet degeneracy with future lensed SNe Ia will also require a detailed reconstruction of discs and dark matter substructures in the lenses.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=118349811 id=\"118349811\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We have evaluated the effect of microlensing on GLSNe Ia for various image configurations, corresponding to values of the convergence \u03ba, the shear \u03b3, and the smooth matter fraction <em>s</em>, across multiple time intervals. We have found that there are regions of parameter space where the effect of microlensing is suppressed enough for the GLSN Ia to be standardizable. Specifically, regions of low \u03ba, \u03b3, and high <em>s</em> are subject to microlensing scatter of \u03c3<sub>ML</sub> \u2272 0.15, particularly at early times (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>). Physically this corresponds to asymmetric configurations with at least one image located far outside the Einstein radius, which will experience the least amount of microlensing.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Combining our microlensing models with the GLSNe Ia catalogue from Goldstein et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), we predict that \u223c22\u00a0per\u2009cent of the \u223c930 GLSNe Ia to be discovered by LSST will be standardizable. From the sample of 650 GLSNe Ia, of which accurate time delays can be measured, the mass-sheet degeneracy can be broken at the 0.5\u00a0per\u2009cent level. The LSST GLSNe Ia sample will thus be robust against systematics in <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> at the 0.5\u00a0per\u2009cent level. The assumed fraction of standardizable systems with accurate time delays may be somewhat pessimistic, since we found that standardizable GLSNe have larger Einstein radii (median 0.9 arcsec) and time delays (median 44\u00a0d), than the general population.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Our result assumes a SN Ia light profile that expands at a constant velocity of 10<sup>4</sup> km s<sup>\u22121</sup>. Whilst simple, more complicated models can be extracted from our results by rescaling the time axis. We have not considered sources with clumpy profiles, however, since the standardizable region of Fig. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> varies only weakly with time, our results should not be heavily influenced by the choice of source model. If the supernova profile contains any small, bright, fast moving clumps then additional scatter may be introduced. However, microlensing of such clumps would introduce rapid temporal variation in the light curve which should be easy to detect.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Whilst this paper does not focus on the IMF, we found a sharp sensitivity to the IMF for lenses with Einstein radii between 0.2 and 0.5 arcsec, assuming a lens and source with the same redshifts as in iPTF16geu. Measuring the scatter in a sample of such GLSNe Ia should trivially discriminate between the Salpeter and Chabrier fits of Auger et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We also applied our microlensing analysis to the GLSN Ia iPTF16geu and compared our results against the More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) analysis, who found a strong discrepancy between the observations and their lens model, attributing the discrepancy to microlensing. Our analysis suggests that the discrepancy cannot be due to microlensing primarily (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig8\" data-open=\"fig8\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">8</a>) and signals potential deficiencies in the use of simple lens macromodels, as suggested by More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This work shows that it is possible to infer the intrinsic luminosity for a significant sample of \u223c 200 LSST GLSNe Ia, suppressing the mass-sheet degeneracy of the lens model. This will allow for accurate and precise measurements of <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> with significantly reduced systematics through time delay cosmography, thus enabling a stringent test of the \u039bCDM model of cosmology.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=118349818 id=\"118349818\" class=\"backfootnotegroup-title\" >Footnotes</h2>\r\n<div content-id=\"fn1\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn1\" class=\"end-note-link\">1</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\">\u03ba is composed of both stellar and dark matter components.</p></div></span></div><div content-id=\"fn2\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn2\" class=\"end-note-link\">2</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\">More et\u00a0al. content-id=\"bib11\" data-legacy-id=\"bib11\"><div class=\"refLink-parent\"><span class=\"refLink\"><a name=\"jumplink-bib11\" href=\"javascript:;\" aria-label=\"jumplink-bib11\"></a></span></div><div We find that the discrepancies between the observed and macromodel predicted fluxes of the other three images are consistent with microlensing."}, "Status": "Complete", "Link": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/link_gateway/2018MNRAS.478.5081F/PUB_HTML", "Pandas format": {"Table 2": {"Action": "Processed via pandas", "Status": "Complete", "Inspection": {"Notes": {"Message on table quality": "image info", "Skip cause table not important": ""}}}}}}, "Paper Overview": {"authors": ["Foxley-Marrable, Max", "Collett, Thomas E.", "Vernardos, Georgios", "Goldstein, Daniel A.", "Bacon, David"], "journal_name": "Monthly Notices of the Royal Astronomical Society", "type_of_reference": "JOUR", "abstract": "We investigate the effect of microlensing on the standardization of strongly lensed Type Ia supernovae (GLSNe Ia). We present predictions for the amount of scatter induced by microlensing across a range of plausible strong lens macromodels. We find that lensed images in regions of low convergence, shear and stellar density are standardizable, where the microlensing scatter is \u2272 0.15 mag, comparable to the intrinsic dispersion of a typical SN Ia. These standardizable configurations correspond to asymmetric lenses with an image located far outside the Einstein radius of the lens. Symmetric and small Einstein radius lenses (\u2272 0.5 arcsec) are not standardizable. We apply our model to the recently discovered GLSN Ia iPTF16geu and find that the large discrepancy between the observed flux and the macromodel predictions from More et al. cannot be explained by microlensing alone. Using the mock GLSNe Ia catalogue of Goldstein et al., we predict that \u223c22 per cent of GLSNe Ia discovered by Large Synoptic Survey Telescope (LSST) will be standardizable, with a median Einstein radius of 0.9 arcsec and a median time delay of 41 d. By breaking the mass-sheet degeneracy the full LSST GLSNe Ia sample will be able to detect systematics in H<SUB>0</SUB> at the 0.5 per cent level.", "doi": "10.1093/mnras/sty1346", "start_page": "5081", "number": "4", "publication_year": "2018/08/1", "end_page": "5090", "custom1": "eprint: arXiv:1802.07738", "author_address": ["AA(Institute of Cosmology and Gravitation, University of Portsmouth, Dennis Sciama Building, Burnaby Road, Portsmouth, PO1 3FX, UK), AB(Institute of Cosmology and Gravitation, University of Portsmouth, Dennis Sciama Building, Burnaby Road, Portsmouth, PO1 3FX, UK), AC(Kapteyn Astronomical Institute, University of Groningen, P.O. Box 800, NL-9700 AV Groningen, the Netherlands; Centre for Astrophysics &amp; Supercomputing, Swinburne University of Technology, PO Box 218, Hawthorn, Victoria, 3122, Australia), AD(Department of Astronomy, University of California, Berkeley, CA 94720, USA; Lawrence Berkeley National Laboratory, Berkeley, CA 94720, USA), AE(Institute of Cosmology and Gravitation, University of Portsmouth, Dennis Sciama Building, Burnaby Road, Portsmouth, PO1 3FX, UK)"], "keywords": ["gravitational lensing: strong", "gravitational lensing: micro", "supernovae: general", "supernovae: individual: iPTF16geu", "cosmological parameters", "cosmology: observations", "Astrophysics - Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics", "Astrophysics - Astrophysics of Galaxies"], "url": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2018MNRAS.478.5081F", "volume": "478", "Title": "The impact of microlensing on the standardization of strongly lensed Type Ia supernovae", "issn": "0035-8711"}}
